et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	 Et les opérations sont telles que vous agissez sur la bouche du malade, et assurez-vous que sa tête soit stable, et élèvez sa langue.
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	 Ensuite, coupez le nerf facial, tant que la langue soit délogée de son état normal, et s'il y a desdouces ou des noeuds, c'est une plaie profonde, alors introduisez l’unciné et coupez soigneusement.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	 Et assurez-vous que la déchirure ne soit pas trop étroite près de là où l'artère se trouve.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	 Et après cela, soulevez la langue rougeâtre et molle, ou froide, puis insérez sous la langue un tampon en lin.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 And let the lice bite the patient every night so that his joints cannot settle.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	 If bleeding occurs, then apply vinegar-soaked lead over it.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	 If the blood does not stop, then cauterize with a long-burning cautery, which is good for this.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 Then apply another treatment until it becomes healthy again.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	 And if you see that it is of a different color or black or hardened, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	 And if it is decaying and swollen with moisture, then apply the oncinic bandage, which has a subtle odor, and release from both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	 And if the bleeding does not stop at your work, then apply sulfur paste until it becomes firm, and return to your work as long as you have treated everything.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then raise the limb with ease and skill, and treat other injuries as needed until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	by sore lese ire ou d’or is a l’in such as both, that et cure it even, and your own teisso; and m both est and the e is the lier. And so and of and swell too much leu si on les de la testee is and s and then oint eau or they are treated with salt and reactions and a tu heal of to l’est et les, and if themes; and both lese est, and the cure;
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	 Never does the condition of swollen throat occur which is called 'godath,' and these are properly referred to as two almonds; when treating them, as we have explained in the section, if they do not heal, be cautious.
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 If it is an abscess that's small and has a flat color, don't probe with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	 And if it is red and the root is large, also don't probe with iron for the bleeding.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	 but let it remain until it's matured, and then you shall divide it, or it may break on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 If it is of pale red color and the roots are fine, prepare the instrument for coping, but first examine if the abscesses rest and are soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	 Then have the patient sit in front of the sun with their eyes shut and mouth open, as you work on them, gripping their temples between your hands, and press their tongue out from under all instruments so that it takes shape.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 and be of silver or fine iron just like a razor blade:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	 You should be pressing the tongue against all this instrument and observe the abscess. Take the needle and insert it into its core, pulling fluid out as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	 And treat any wound with cloths, then apply the bandage using an instrument of which this shape seems like a force.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 And thusly the head is bent, with one side higher than the other, and it's very painful, made of iron or bandage.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	 And it has a sharp edge on one side and no name on the other.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And when you have bandaged one of the almonds (referring to parts of the body or perhaps metap#160metaphors), then bandage the other in the same manner. After making an incision, gargle the patient with warm water and saltwater for ease; if bleeding occurs, continue gargling with warm water until the bleeding stops. Alternatively, use juice from cooked pomegranates or crushed myrtle leaves.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then treat until it becomes healthy again;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 And no other abscesses appear in the throat except for two almonds, if they occur as such like the two almonds themselves.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, which is to say, one small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 and had closed off the entire throat so well that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she stayed like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swoln that it had been pushed through both nostrils by the two openings of the small one.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	 So I did so immediately, and inserted an ivy cone therein, then the thread was pulled through, and a great portion of wax came out.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	 Then rejoin it on the other side through the nostrils, and open the mouth and compress the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	 After inserting the needle into the abscesses, and taking some material from it, but did not obtain much blood.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	 And thus they dilated the woman's throat passage, and began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop trying to remove that abscess for long periods of time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	 And the abscesses returned again and filled up with what I had emptied from them until they became quite large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	 Then I deceived him and cauterized inside his throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	 So he stopped growing.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 And from these parts, and only God did anything to him afterwards.
de l’uve	them. 7-30.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	 When they attempt to return it to its place, and it is inflamed and long, then call it "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 And if it is very large and round, then call it an "eyeball".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	 When it is treated as we have described in the section, and the treatment yields no benefit, and you see that the abscess has calmed down but is subtle, then it must be excised.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	 And those that are round and not elongated.
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 And if it is of blood or fishy color or blackish, then one should avoid making an incision in it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	 Therefore, when you see it as I have described regarding its appearance and length, make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument we previously mentioned.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Then insert the needle into the vein, withdraw it slightly, and follow the procedure for two small incisions as previously mentioned for incision of the stones.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	 And it is necessary that you do not fill more than what lies beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	 for if you fill too much, it causes pain to the voice and speech.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 and after the incision, follow what we have said in the incision of the stones, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient fears being covered, then you must apply an instrument for the reassurance of the cover.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 The manner of this cautery is acute ague.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	 And it is that the patient places his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue with the instrument as we have said in the fire cautery treatise, and rinse with lively fresh water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And with this instrument, here is its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	 And it has a handle or hollow where the medicine is placed, like the handles of a spoon, and places the instrument with all the medicine under the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	 and let the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth containing the medicine inside, ensuring it does not descend to the throat and belly.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	 then hold your hand with all the medicine and press it against the eye, a quantity about half an hour's worth, until you see movement easing and the bitterness of the medicine is soothed.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	 and if you see this, take some cotton and wrap it around any instrument, dampen the cotton with the medicine, and place the instrument onto all the cotton in the canal above, until the cotton becomes moist on the eye.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	 And often do this until the cautery is perfected, then let it dry, and falls off after IV or V days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	 And if you need to repeat the medicinal caustication, upon repeating it, and after caustication around the eye, use a cotton soaked in butter, and cleanse what is surrounding the medicinal area.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And be raised from cold water, and be healed by gargling until it feels normal again.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	 This treatment is more about the incision, not just the caustication.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	 If it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamine and wormwood and origanum (oregano) and rue (herb), and chamomile and avronne (horseradish) and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of these into a pot, set it to ease, and make boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 And let the bone be well fixed with strong clay, and within the hole have an instrument fitted according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	 And be it of silver or iron, and let one of the heads be placed in the mouth of the patient until the vapors rise to the eye through the canal, until the vein is constricted.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	 after its recurrence often, until the vein dries, and ensure that you do not touch it at the beginning of the emergence of the hot abscess, for many things can happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 and do not touch it when it is in the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	 And if this instrument is not present, take a canal and put in its head an eagle's feather so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 For the crack of a tooth does not greatly affect the breathing through the mouth, and it is good healing together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	 Often, one may feel something in the throat or spine of a fish, or anything else.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	 Therefore, if it is necessary to examine what you can see, and press the tongue to the sunlight along the entire instrument, so that you may observe any movement.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	 And what does not open and is returned to the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit at this point as well, so that the meat may be cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	 In case the thing has been expelled through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	 Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of thread, or a lettuce root, or crust from dry bread.
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	 And tie it to the sponge or thread, and then swallow it again.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	 And when it reaches the stomach, if it dissolves, then drain the fluid;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 And if it does not come out as we have said, then take a tool of bone as described here:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	 And raise the instrument's handle so it can more easily enter the throat, and keep the head raised high.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	 And be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so it does not close, nor insert the bone too deeply.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	 And to move it means the patient touches the instrument, because it is out of place or unnatural.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 If desired, where he traces with all instruments evenly until firm.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of throat constriction
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	 Never is there a treatment without suction, as I have said in the section, through medical treatments;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 And when this does not help, then look in the throat of the patient towards the sun, and then press his tongue with the instrument I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see stiffness, treat it entirely with small pincers or delicate forceps that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that is not effective, then take a hollow reed, and put it into the patient's throat, and repeatedly perform warm compresses with the heated iron rod, as often as necessary.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if you give the patient water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	 Then take full sip of cold water and work the mouth, and it produces the urge to swallow, and often moves with its hand.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 And as soon as suction feels the water, it flows.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	 If it does not come out as we have said, then smoke the patient with strong onion using the instrument mentioned in the fumigation of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 Do this many times, for it will burn very sore.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	 And the manner of fumigation is that you shall have a pot with coal embers in it, and place under a cloth sieve through which the head should be inserted using the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	 Then pour your fumes, and the patient puts their head in a container with their mouth closed so that no smoke enters but reaches up to the eyes.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	 And now the eye will begin to burn, and if it does not come out, restart the fumigamination many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	 And sufferers experience thirst, and consume salted and sour things, and do not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 Then it becomes necessary for him to be released under this regimen.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	 And the form of the instrument with which one treats swelling is, when it can be seen, similar to crooked tongs designed for entering into the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	 and it resembles the beak of a physician's tool, and there is roughness of lime, such that whatever it grasps, it cannot release.
et vez ci la forme:	 and so this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The form of the instrument that looks like it must not be swallowed. And here is a healer, and here.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	 There are many forms of abscesses, as the memory comes to this and that in this book, and they differ between perforation and cutting.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 And there are two ways of which one is as it appears itself, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is for boils which occur within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For an abscess in the head is different from that at the base, and an abscess of the shoulder blade is different from those occurring in joints, and each has its judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	 And if at an abscess we should not pierce, until the bowel is fully matured according to its completion.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 and if of such that it must be pierced when they are ripe, do not die according to their completion, as abscesses which are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When an abscess occurs near the joints and is left to rot therein, on occasion it may be so that the tissue and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	 Or if an abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay the piercing until it is matured, harm will come to the main limb.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	 or if it is near the base, then one should pierce as soon as it is matured.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	 and it should not be pierced without completed digestion, except for those near the base, that it may not burst forth too quickly, extend inwardly, and become a fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 And cannot heal completely.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	 And it is necessary that you know the time of abscess perforation when healing progresses, and when pain eases, departure of fever, diminution of swelling and redness, and faint debates and sharpening of the abscess head, and other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	 And it is necessary to wait for some time after the perforation or as long as needed from the abscess site, and where movement occurs.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 And the perforation should be long in duration for the body, and if the abscess is on hands or feet, or at joints and veins, and at arteries, in all cases where there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 When they swell, according to which limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in the churned flesh, you must allow the opening to remain until it is fully healed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	 If you pierce it before this spot, there is venom running through his body, and it is filled with much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 And sometimes the lips harden and the deepest parts of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And for any abscess that you perceive according to the width of its body, as befits the limb it is in.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	 And it is necessary for you to treat small abscesses and small wounds.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	 and in large abscesses, large wounds, and many ruptures according to the appearance of the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	 and if with such abscesses it is necessary to cut the flesh, and cover them up.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	 when they become just like rags, and are moldy, then it must be done as with barrels.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	 and if there are those that are split into three corners, and if so with such as are covered like the bellows of mire, like hookworms.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And if there are such places where one makes a round incision, or other cuts and similar injuries.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	 For those without heads, as with superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them straight through;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	 and when the abscess is large, with great swelling, and you pierce it, do not drain all of the pus in that hour, but rather a part of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	 then probe the abscess until the next day, and then fully drain it.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	 do this repeatedly, gradually more each time, until all of the swelling subsides.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 especially if the patient is weak in vigor, or a woman carrying, or small children, or elderly and infirm men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the arrow can sometimes leap out with the release of the bowstring, and inadvertently kill the patient, so be cautious.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	 Discharge this chapter with great care, and when you have detected your abscess, drain the wound, and examine if the wound from the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	 And if it is a neatly sized one, then dress with either linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	 And if it is large abscesses and there are many outgrowths, then one should dress each with a bandage so they may come into contact with each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	 And if you have cut into the abscess near the skin, and removed it entirely, then fill it with old cotton or flax cloth without moisture, and bind until the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then consult a doctor, and apply ointment as long as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 If bleeding occurs on your wound, treat with cold water and ease, and moist cloth, and place it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	 If the bleeding persists, if it is well-managed and cared for, and the powders I have mentioned in this book are used, and if it is winter or when the affected area or abscess is very inflamed, then you must apply warm woolen tents and linens soaked in wine and hot oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	 If it is summer and the affected area or wound is fleshly, then you must apply warm linens soaked in water and oil, or wine and cold oil, until the third day as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then release the abscess and drain it, and treat it as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	 This must be known universally in treating abscesses:

des soros	Of pus-filled collections.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 When small abscesses arise in the scalp, they are handled as silk, similar to the follicles of a girl's hair, and there are many like this.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	 There are those that are greasy and sticky like hairs.
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 And if there are such things that are hard and thorny at the tail, then there is no doubt as long as the arrow does not go against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the techniques of bandaging are such that you must try with all instruments called 'entromissors', from which formations come afterwards and what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Because if it contains moisture, it grows above the long one. (This could refer to a growth or formation that occurs when there is an excess of moisture.)
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	 And when the moisture is emptied, scrape without leaving any hair that contains it, for it returns as soon as you leave nothing behind.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	 Then dip a piece of cotton in Egyptian salve if available.
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	 If not, use water and salt, and apply the balm to the wound, leaving it until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And thus will run those who are displaced during the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	 And then begin the wrapping again, as before, on the second day and third, until you are certain that it does not dislocate at night.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the wound with ointment as suitable for him, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	 And if an abscess persists, then apply this according to this form, in the long manner;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	 and collect thy pus, and scrape away all scabs, and apply your healing treatment to the sore as it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the arrow causes him pain in return, do what I have told you afterward.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And similarly treat an abscess if it is pus-filled, and with scraping and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And the treatment of a pus-filled abscess and its moisture is easier, for it contains less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	 And if any of these abscesses or heads without moisture are present, and those old-fashioned ones that I have described at the head.
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	 And I found the abscess like a hard stone, sharp and bruised, which could not be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 But if one had hit it with anything, they would have made a wound like from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	 In other abscesses coming or at the top, such as those that come from the top of children's heads and rooting in their ears, open it daily near the most dependent point, so that pus may exit.
et les cure si com il covient.	 and treat them as needed.
des scrophules	Of scrofulous tumors
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Many times these abscesses occur on the neck, and from under the shoulders, and in the armpits, and never come to any other place or body parts, and they are very much, and closely connected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	 And each scrofula properly forms within its quarter, like the knot and the top abscess, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 and the similarities of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and others that hold malicious intentions which do not wish to obey healthiness.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	 in that one then which you see of good bodily arrangement at the touch, and is similar to the color of the body overall, and moves from all sides and not so loose on the skin nor veins nor arteries or vessels, and it's not deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	 If it is necessary to treat it from above, and peel off each part, extend the two lips double the thickness of the nail, if needed, as we have said in head sores.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 And move it little by little, and be sure not to cut the nerve or vein, nor is it necessary to remove the spatula or cutting tool, lest the hand slips and does too much before you need to stop when necessary.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	 And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not bleed, place vitriol paste in the wound, or any powders that coagulate blood, and bind the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 and let it rest until the sore is soothed, and made softened, and begins to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	 And when the blood is stopped, return to your work until you have completed it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 Then go back to your proper course if there are small tumors remaining after some time; treat and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	 And if the blood vessel at the root of a tumor is large, do not just excise that tumor at its base but instead tie it with strong double thread and let it hang without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 Then dress the wound with well-boiled cotton soaked in Egyptian salve, then bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you completely remove the scrofula, it is necessary to bring together the two edges of the wound and hold them closed now, so that there is no excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 And it is necessary for you to bind up the root and drain pus, and close as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	 For tumors that cause excess, puncture where they come to an end;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	 and do the same as previously described, then clean it with salve and other similar things if there is decay present.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the wound is thoroughly cleaned, apply a poultice of soaking oil until it heals.
de squinance	If you are treated by applying a tissues to ensure there's no longer remains of any dead tissue, then as we had said previously mentioned, so forth; and when the wound with substances so is that healing ointment and other until it properly cleaned becomes cured.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	 The ancients spoke and wrote about throat surgery.
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 But I have never seen it done in our land, and it is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	 For those with stridor, it is necessary to clear out the incision in the throat called "epiglottis".
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 And no aid is provided through this method because all the veins and the evil humors of the body are found in those with abscesses burning hotly within the mouth, throat or arms.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the main source, it is necessary to remove the epiglote to avoid destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	 Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should make an incision just above or below three circles or four from one side as a small slit lengthwise between two circles or along the quantity of the fissure, but not into the trachea.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 And those who are so sore have their section of the epiglottis performed where there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	 And if the master is fearful, it must be stretched with skin from the throat to its full length, then cut the flesh until reaching the windpipe.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	 and remove the blood vessels, if you see nothing else, then close the sac as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	 and demonstrated by the section of the windpipe vein that tears apart when it is ruptured where the voice fails.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 and leave the open wound exposed for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	 And when there is doubt about strangulation after some time has passed, gather the two lips of the wound in the throat area and suture all together until the cartilage is felt.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then administer medicines that generate heat, until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	the uzerd: and  (or they:s.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	 Then place a covering over the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, thus preventing death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	 and so they instruct the patient to leave the wound open until the illness is gone, which takes 3 or 4 days; then they command it be sewn shut and treated, until healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 And I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	 I saw a maiden take a knife and plunge it into her throat, cutting part of the tongue.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 And so they called me to heal her, finding her almost dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I examined the wound and found that blood had come from it; however, she hadn't bitten a vein or other tissue, just her throat, and the blood flow was coming through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	 I addressed it quickly, sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	 and nothing of this occurred to the lady except that her voice turned red, and she recovered afterward into her own condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 for I tell you that in treating the epiglottis there is no need to fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	 These abscesses are called "throat hernias," and they are large abscesses the color of jet black, and occur mostly in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	 and there are two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	 natural, and accidental.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 or naturally, it has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	 And the accidental one is in two ways: one seems like fat to us, and the other way it resembles an abscess that comes from our arteries.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	 When there is fear, and it does not matter to work on external things except in that which is small, and test and search for everything involved.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	 If you find it as we have learned, and do not apply to any vein, if the bandage is applied as one would bind wounds, and treat the entire area, if there are points.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And search thoroughly, and heal it as necessary, until it is perfectly well again.
des nous	And let us know.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	 There are many ways to us, of which I will say all the variations;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 And here I must explain all the differences between them and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	 I say that dislocation is accompanied by heat and fever until the boiling has passed, and tissue destruction is complete.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 Then rests the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	 With ours there is no heat or fever nor pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and according to the body's color, beginning like glass and becoming larger.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 And they follow II similarities, or grease, or moisture, and the colors are as I have mentioned in the section.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the care of us that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "intermitted", according to its form or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	 And the method of inquiring about abscesses in us is that you extract or find more moisture than you see in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little until you know that the discharge has reached the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 Then extract the intramedullary bone, and take care so it does not break.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	 If there is a running discharge through the skin, if its color matches what I have said about other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	 And if there is no discharge after extracting the intramedullary bone, it indicates fatty tissue, then cut accordingly in a cross pattern, and grasp with forceps, and lightly scrape from each side, and cover the cloth where it lies to treat it cleanly with needlework.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 And if you cannot treat it cleanly, then cut in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	 Because if anything remains, it will return to you many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if it remains a bit and does not bother you, apply the wound with some corrosive powders, tighten the wound, and put in soothing substances to treat other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 And if they are large, cut the two edges of the wound, and treat as though burned by a hot liquid.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	 And if the burn from scraping is opposite or different, quickly apply the lead of antimony paste, and let it rest for two days or three, until the wound heals, and allow time for blood to replenish.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 Then return to using what was previously left out because of this.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	 See here the forms of interposed suppurations, and there are three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	 large, medium, and small.
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	 And among them are three types called "albarata", one type is called "rebebo," and there are three kinds.
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	 large, means, small, to search for abscesses of a fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	 and they are like needles with which one pierces the sorcery, made of citrine stone, iron or silver, whose movement is valued as that which is yellow, and more tested for searching blisters of a fistula by black bumps.
et sont de III manieres:	 and they are in three ways:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	 The forms of tumors are mostly similar, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	 large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	 and for tumors that have two blisters in three ways also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	 and for tumors that have three blisternails are found under the skin. They resemble small lumps or pimples in different sizes according to the size of their openings. There are large, medium, and small vari
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	 And if there are knots with two horns, and knots of one horn only, and they come in three kinds.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 And all these are necessary at their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	 The head of these that are sharp is cutting, and some do not cut other than one side, from which we scrape the skin, so the vein nor nerve is severed.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	 and these intruders are reset in layers, so that the patient does not suffer at the onset of boils.
et sont de III manieres:	 And they come in three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	 large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	 And they are not used anywhere else but in the joints of legs and arms, breasts, shoulders, and similar areas.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 And at no other time is another instrument made small, resembling the sharpened sticks of lancets, according to this method, which punctures blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed at no time back into its proper position of veins and arteries, and does not return according to this grand form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	 At no time do the breasts of any man swell when he begins to be corrupted, until they resemble a woman's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 and remain ugly and swolled, and those who wish to treat them must do so according to this method of the treatment line; b. until g: (The latter part seems incomplete or unclear in Old French, possibly referring to a specific section or page number.)
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 then scrape the fat, and dress the wound with cleaning clay, then stitch together the two edges of the wound by sewing, and let it heal until it is healthy.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	 And if it inclines forward, becoming weakened due to its size like it often occurs in women, causing pain in the ribs above, by two similar tears.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	 For this is why one hangs from the other at each end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b. up to line g.

et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	 And if it is not clean or the incision isn't fully made because the patient doesn't want to rest, or due to blood loss, then you must fill the wound with a cloth of compressed cotton in a corrosive salve.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 And he leaves it to settle until it reattaches and absorbs fat, then treats it so that it becomes clean.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses and fractures of the arms and legs
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that arise from the limbs are hard sores or ulcers, and some that contain pus.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Those which contain moisture must be cut following this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	an:
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to hard tumors, treat them as we have described in cutting open hard tumors, and if the wound reopens, prepare the fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	For rupturing of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	 When the vein is torn and the skin is sutured on top of it, often there are many abscesses, and similarly, blood vessels bleed and become infected.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	 And if the cone is placed in this way for the artery, then the abscesses are large at their origin;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	 And when you touch it on your elbebows, it feels extremely painful.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	 and if it is for the vein, then there are often visible bulges appearing;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 It is foolish to try and cover this abscess, especially when it lies beneath the nails and joints and where there are many other openings, and they are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	 Therefore it is necessary to remove the iron bandage, and those who are at the neck must also have it removed, and in those with swelling of arteries above the long skin.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	 then work on the tonsils, and carefully release the vessel from the sutures, until it is fully exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	 then insert a needle from underneath it and pierce through to the other side, and secure the vessel with a double thread in two loops, as I have shown you during the extraction of the two vessels located in the temple.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	 then make a hole between the two loops with an introducer until no blood flows from it, and release the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	 Then apply a bandage to reduce swelling until it subsides.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then apply an ointment suitable for this, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	 And if an abscess is due to the size of the vein, it must be treated with ointment that you can apply to all over the affected skin, then insert the needle from where you hold in your hand and pierce it completely through the skin, making sure to use double thread as you pass it across.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	 Then treat the abscess as I have instructed, or if possible at both ends of the double thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	 And if you doubt that the threads are not strong enough, then insert another needle through all of it from the incision made by the first needeled and pull out both ends in four lengths.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	 Then cover the abscess until excess tissue forms, then remove the excess flesh and leave what remains.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then apply a poultice of wool in wine and oil, then treat with bandages and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	From abscesses to nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in arteries and veins, they also appear on nerves when struck or from excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	 And this occurs often in shoulders and elbebows where there are joints, and they have serious abscesses, their color resembles that of the body, and they cause pain in various ways.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	 And when it is pressed firmly, it causes the patient great pain, but not throughout the body, rather away from the core.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	 And it is moved equally in all directions; neither forward nor backward, up nor down, and those with joint issues should not be bound with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	 Perhaps they would go against it;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And those who are at the head or forehead create ruptures in the dura mater.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	 If abscesses are small, if you have pincers, and cover it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if they are large, use a hook to extract it, then scrape and suture the wound, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Large hanging sores
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	 It never occurs in limbs and not elsewhere, and it is an illness called "fungus" due to its appearance, and the roots are fine, but the head is large.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	 and there are both small and very large ones.
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 And I saw in the home two stomachs that were more fungus-like than anything else, with no differences, they were white, had fine roots, and were split, causing excessive moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	 I weighed them and found in one eighteen ounces, and in the other six, and the work of incision should be such that you examine if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist with a fine root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 If it breaks to the spatulum wide, and there are in your presence the fire cautery.
