et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	 And then you constrain it, and continue to strain the thread of wax until it fits the articular cavity, and thus work is done through it.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	 And if the roots are large, be wary of using it in one sitting for fear of burdening the stomach, but do well to cover most of it, then cauterize so it does not return.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 Then treat the wound and ensure that you do not cover the thole which is of sickly color and poor sense and lacking regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is an encrusted boil, and I will come to treat this syphilis hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the mouth is forcibly closed.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	 If the appearance of gangrene comes from cauterization of a wound or fistula opening and is around the abd [domain] without swelling, as it occurs in other regions, or bleeding from veins or arteries according to what lies before, or edema;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 And if it is by the rupture of the sinew and the exit of the bile, then the color of the abscess appears similar to that of the body's flesh, and it is a slight matter without pain, open from various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then there are various outcomes; and when one presses on its extremities, it recoils, then returns, and at times it may be hardened, with significant enlargement at the entrance of the bowel for intense work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and open well when you apply pressure with your hand, do not constrain.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	 And if it is due to blood, then the abscess opens through these signs large and hard, and it adheres according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to inflammation, then it is tender upon touching, and the evacuations are such that you observe whether the appearance is from blood of an artery, or a vein, or inflammamenent.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 If it is necessary to leave the healing alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter of abscesses, for arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	 And if the appearance is for the intestines or the belly, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to dip his finger, and be extended straight up, then tie all around the bowels.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	 Then command him to lie supine between your hands, then go around the limb that you have tied at all the spermatic veins, then extend half of the abscess above all along the large penis.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	 Then bind it with a strong thread or a cord of sturdy silk firmly, and be sure not to loosen the ligation.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	 Then work on extending half of the abscess above the ligature and apply your mustard plaster, then envelop the intestines.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	 If you find it caught by the ligament, if you dislocate it, and put the intestines back into place through the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	 And if you find that there is swelling, if you grasp the tendon, and remove the excess fluid.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	 And if the artery is acting against you, or it pulsates, and runs out abundantly, then return to your work and take two needles, insert them in a cross-shaped pattern where you previously made an incision.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	 Then stretch the abscess in four directions above the needles and if you see it, remove the neednails, and let them remain until they heal, and drain any necrotic tissue.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	 When you may the cow with its udder under and plucked, then treat as necessary, and when the abscess occurs as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And extract any blood or pus that you find, then treat the wound as necessary, and sew it shut.
dou chancre	Of burning sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	 We have said in that section the similarities of syphilis, and how one should work with remedies, and how to purge the bloodletting.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	 And say the syphilis erupts in the skin, and great caution is needed for treatment, and our ancestors said that when syphilis appears on an exposed area or can be removed like warts in armpits, groin, and similar areas, it should all be excised at the beginning.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	 And when it is large and old, you must not approach it at all, for I have never been able to heal any.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 nor has anyone ever been healed by me before.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	 And the procedure, when it is in place or can be removed as we have said, involves emptying any black pus from the patient.
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	 then cleanse the wound if there is evident swelling, and prepare the patient properly to perform the procedure.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	 then pour in your suppurating sores or ulcers, and any flesh at their base, and the bone without leaving anything.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 and allow the blood to flow freely, pressing firmly with your hand or another object, and if the spread of blood is opposite to the incision in an artery or vein, cauterize until it ceases.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat with another treatment until it is set right.
de ydropisie	From dropsy (edema)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	 We have said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is formed, the signs of each kind, and the treatment made by medicines, and that which is treated with iron.
si est eclites soulement;	 if it only swells up;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	 and one should not touch with iron in these two kinds;
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	 that is to say, tympanites and hyposarca, because it's a deadly thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	 Therefore, when you treat this resemblance of dropsy called "swelling" with medicines and the treatment does not help, look to see if the patient is weak or has another illness besides drops지, as well as vomiting and similar things.
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	 If you do not use iron, for there is doubt.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	 And if you see the patient in good physical condition and has no other illness but dropsy alone, and is neither too young nor too old, then work thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 Lift the patient upright with your hands, and the assistant presses the belly, pushing water to the lowest part of the groin, then take the spinous-spatula as follows:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And so employ sharp instruments of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	 At an angle, and always ensure that it does not go too deep until reaching the intestines when inserted. Do not spill it:
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	 Then look to see if dropsy has settled toward the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	 If it is necessary, you should insert into the bowel on the side III directly above the elbow.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	 If it is dropsy due to a liver disease, make an incision on the left side of the groin II inches.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	 And if it is due to an ulcer, make the incision on the right side, and it must only be so that the patient lies above the incision where excess fluids do not flow to that weak spot.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	 Then penetrate the skin with the instrument and stop it, and lift your hand to cover all of the tissue between the skin and fascia as when scraping for an amount equal to that of a fingernail or slightly more.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 Then penetrate the fascia until you reach the level of eight tissues, and it is the source of water; then proceed further, and stop with this instrument which has this shape.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	 It resembles a subtle silver chain, and is made of silk or light linen, and in the part below the small eyelet.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	 and it has a stitch on one side, three loops.
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	 and two on the other side, one in the center;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 It is shaped as a pen tip, and it's the shape of the incision that the writer makes to cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	 at the top underneaturally, so when it becomes moistened with water, they descend upon the instrument now.
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	 empty the majority or one-third of it because if you empty more than is needed at that time, by chance the patient may die due to exhaustion from holding their spirit against the weapon, as they sweat profusely, or approach death.

puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	 Then continue with the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering such symptoms, and draw a small quantity of water.

And the care of medicinal desiccants until it is dry enough, and cauterization over the stomach and liver and spleen after fluid extraction, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of erecting the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 There is never a child born with no foreskin on the penis, or if present, it is small, or not in its proper place.

et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 And perhaps nothing is needed in that case because the strong flow of urine leaves no blockage behind.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 If it is found that his urinary tract is small, then it is indeed the medicine of a lead plug as we have said, which will enlarge.

de la circoncision	For circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	 Circumcision is not a disjunction of continuity like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 However, when we perform this work of our own free will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the easiest for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they do not practice it in their laws, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	 Because I want to include the greatest part of masters and saints who performed circumcision before me on the organ, the strength, and everything anew;

et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 and with the cleansing of the nail by chance it escapes from the iron, and worms burrow in, and many times they emerge thus there is no need for further cleansing and I have witnessed this.

From the trimming which is done using force on all parts of the sinew, I have found the benefit of experimentation, as the force cuts equally well above and below.

Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	 The shape of the forceps for cleaning is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 Both ends of the forceps should be held and sharp, and the jaws as large as the pincers uniformly:

dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	 The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or frozen blood, or bowel, or foreign object, which we have discussed in that section.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	 And if the urine is not flowing freely, and you see retention due to a stone that is located at the bladder neck or urethra, then it requires that the patient be placed on their side with knees bent.

et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And repeat with the syringe as long as his bladamo is emptied, and settle the male's issue.
des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When incontinence or blood appears within the bladder, with pus accumulating there and you see to distill waters and medicines, do all that is called "clêpesdre," which is its form.
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	 It is closed, and if at three holes:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	 Part one, and part two, as you see.
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	 And the tools with which the medicinal cord is such that it properly fills the wound without addition, and if possible to drain the moisture, and apply as needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	 And when you see your medicines in the bladder, place the head of the catheter where it should be to drain into the moisture, and leave them as they are.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	 If you draw out the moisture through the catheter, then firmly reset the tube back in place;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	 If more moisture enters there, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	 And this is the form of the subtle enema used for cleansing the bladder:
si est ci:	 If so, then let them lie still; and
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	 And it is of silver or iron, and the head lies higher.
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	 and below the neck where the ligaments tear.
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	 Then take a sheep bladder and place the moisture you wish to apply via enema inside it, then tie it between two breasts with a good double thread, and warm that moisture over fire.

et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	 And if you don't have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make it into a circle, and pierce it roundly through.

de la piere	Stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	 We have discussed in the section the methods of stone removal and arrow extraction together with remedies;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	 And I explained the difference between stones formed by rain, and all other signs, and in which type of stone one must work through cutting.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	 And in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 And I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	 I say that stones formed by urine in the bladeboily often occur in children, and it is a sign that water leaks from the bladder resembling water due to its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	 And it has hairs on its surface, and it weakens the ill person's strength, and they do so many times, and then straighten them out.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	 and to numerous wounds, it affects their foundation;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	 and the healing of children is easy until they reach four years old, it is very severe in the elderly, and moderate for those between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 and its treatment is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with an enema in order to expel all the filth from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For this prevents any time seeking for stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	 Then take the sick person by their feet and stand them up straight, turning so that the stone descends to the front of the bladeback, and sometimes comes out from above.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	 Then make them sit between your hands properly laid, with their hands below their thighs, so that the bladeback is completely inclined downward.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	 Then grasp and touch within.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 If you feel the stone in the space, quickly proceed to cut near the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	 And if it does not come out with the touch, grease your index finger on the left hand with oil, if the patient is a child or an adolescent.

puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 then press with your finger, and push down where you plan to cut.

puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 Then he applies the splinting bandage as follows: which is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	 And it is made between that which lies between the joints and the base, not within but on the left side of the sinew.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	 And it should be straight above the stone, and between your thigh and base, and let the shaft be as wide at its widest part and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	 Occasionally press on that which is between your thigh and base so it feels no strain.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	 And say if there are stones or edges within.
si est griés a issir;	 If the stone is difficult to remove.
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And if it appears soft and round like glue, of which removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	 To make a celi where there are edges and margins, enlarge the incision.
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	 And if it does not come out, then you must extract with tongs similar to a file at the tip, in order to fully remove the stone so that it does not escape.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	 or place your instrument delicately like a curved awl at the top;

et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 and if there are multiple stones, first remove the largest one from the bladder neck, then cut into it, then crush it, and after that, take out any smaller ones that remain.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 If it is very large, one must sear it, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	 For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	 If he dies or his urine returns through the same place because the bones cannot unite.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	 Yet make an effort with milking or using tongs for debridement, until you clean it in pieces.

Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have also found this to be so.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron rod according to this form and it is pierced at four angled tips in one piece:

de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	 Sometimes a stone may be embedded in women, and if this occurs once, it requires careful treatment and is forbidden for three reasons.
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	 one because the woman might possibly be a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 and secondly, we cannot find a maid who is willing to undress in front of strangers, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	 and thirdly, it may be that we cannot find a woman skilled in this art of healing hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	 and fourthly, if the stone in the woman is more deeply embedded than in men, thus it requires deeper cutting, which causes great fear. And if necessary, one must seek a midwife who knows well and has little charge for her services. If you cannot find such a person, there are no guarantees of success with this method.

c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 That is to say, small and large and sharp and smooth, long and round, and with veins.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you examine the similarities to know the outcome.

puis cure la plaie.	 Then treat the wound.

de hernie carnouse	For a carnous hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	 Respite is nothing but an assembly of moisture or white sores, which are from beneath the head of the joints that contain pus.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	 and they are called "syfas", and never properly in the fabric of the pus, if one thinks it is another kind.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	 And this is the proper location of the vein we have mentioned, between the white fibula.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 And it has no other course than that.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the creation of this hernia is due to weakness in the veins, where that matter expands.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	 And never comes from striking on the joints, and this moisture is of many kinds:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	 or it shows a leaning towards jaundice, or it lacks redness, or is black, or watery white, and this occurs more frequently.

Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	 And if there is moisture in the actual fabric, then they are real boils with part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks it's another egg.

des hermofrodites	Hermaphroditism refers to a condition where an individual has both male and female reproductive organs or characteristics of both sexes. This term was derived from Greek mythology, referring to the deity Hermes/Mercury, who was born with combined features of his parents Zeus (the sky god) and Hermah (a nymph). In modern times, it is considered an outdated and potentially offensive term; preferred terms are intersex or transgender.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	 Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways at home:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 One is where between the two openings it appears just as a woman's natural form, and may have hair, or sometimes they urinate.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other manner is in women, and it is above their wrist like a rod and two hoops.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	 And the treatment of the body and flesh is such that you bandage all swellings as with other wounds.
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 In the second way, for men whose urine flows through their thighs' skin, there is no cure.

des emorroides	Hemorrhoids are a condition characterized by swollen veins in the lower rectum and anus areas; it's often due to straining during bowel movements or increased pressure in that region from various causes such as pregnancy, constipation, sitting for long periods. For treatment: encourage gentle hygiene practices to prevent irritation, use of mild soapsuds and avoiding harsh chemicals; recommend softening stool with a diet high-fiber foods like fruits, vegetables, whole grains. dou fremit	In trembling

des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	 We have said in the section on wound treatment;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	 or we will speak of hand and eye treatments, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on what they are made of, and where or how the lacerations or injuries are made, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	 The things by which wounds are made involve cutting with stones or swords and axes, or lances, clubs, or arrows, or similar objects;

ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 These stitches serve as a suture, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his abdomen, which was afflicted by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, with intestines protruding about two palms wide, located within the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I brought back the intestines because it had been fourteen hours since he was injured, and I dressed his wound until the fifteenth day, and cared for him, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	 And the physician judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	 and I did not treat him with ointment because I was in a place where there were none to be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And put a cloth twice daily over the wound, and wash it with honey water until healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	 Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	 Take a needle and pass it through the part forward up to its inner depths;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	 When it has felt the head straight left or right, where you have inserted the needle into its socket or casing, and pierced from another side to within until reaching that far.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 And the understanding of this suture is that you cut it as a tailor would with scissors, and leave one side of the socket once, then rejoin from another until the suture is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	 The second manner of suturing that Galen properly describes is as with those who join two parts together naturally and apply one end of the socket to the other end in such a way.
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	 Pierce with a needle or nearby metal rod and make a cut there only, leaving the two ends of the socket.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	 Then turn the needle, and make it pierce through to the forward part up to inside the socket of the eye.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	 Then make it pierce both forward parts to inside the socket of each eye, in two other eyebrows that are opposite.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 And this is the proper method of suturing and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	 Galen says this word, and no one bears witness to it, that you must sew the abdomen with two needles, each having thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	 and one needle should be inserted from one side, and the other from the opposite, in the manner of those who sew belts.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 And know that when the rupture is within the abdabinee, it must be sutured more carefully than other parts of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	 The judgments of wounds are such as the judgments of other wounds.
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	 and it is that when you find the fresh wound fully supplied with blood, thus as the art directs, reset its intestines and the cord.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	 then apply to it with the powder of jarnac, and if the art has moved it, place any salve that is available until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	 and strip the hairs, then cauterize with tar, honey, and myrrh;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then treat the wound as you would others until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 and if you have no medicine, apply these immediately when the wound starts to close: cotton, and stir it twice daily until healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	 In certain situations, there is no need for additional medicine when wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	 And if you suspect that the wound is affecting proximity to the main members (limbs), it is necessary to gently grind linen in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the limb and underneath the elbow pads.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	 And if it causes pain or swelling in the armpit, which often occurs, apply a black wine enema and particularly when the swelling reaches up to the intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 And proceed with probing, and know that it is easier to heal when it concerns the large intestine than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is distressed, and this is because of the subtlety of its veins throughout the body, and its closeness to one's essence.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	 And if the kidney protrudes from the wound, reset it as well as the intestines while they are fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	 And if it is old and has turned or black, then you must reset the dislocated part that is black, so as to prevent bleeding from vessels and veins.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 Then wrap what is between the joints and hang two belts from below the wound area to ease extraction when splinters are removed, and the wound bandages.
de la routure dou boueil	From the treatment of a boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	 When the intestines are exposed and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in certain cases, as I have seen a man afflicted by an arrow or a stab to the abd([domain])ent.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	 and it was a wound on the right side of the stomach, which became infected and turned into a fistula, causing diarrhea and gas.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 I gave care according to what I could, and did not stop probing until it was healthy again, and the joints were restored.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	 And when I saw it healed, I suspected that the patient still had pain in their stomach;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	 and there was no harm, but they remained in better conditions, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	 and experimentalists said that for small wounds in the intestines, it should be treated in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	 take fat from large kidneys, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the fat has fully closed its mouth, place it under two lips to stretch its mouth out.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	 then wrap the head with bandages and keep it so that it cannot loosen, then place another piece of fat afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is fully healed.
et cout la plaie.	 And observe the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	 The head so swells in the intestines, and causes no harm to the patient, and it is possible to suture the intestine with a fine thread cut from an animal's intestine in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	 Take the head of this thread of intestines that is well cleaned, and then tie it to the end of a fine linen thread twisted tightly, put the thread on the needle, and sew through the intestine, and return the stitch.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	 And this method of suturing aims to be only as strong as trust and hope guides it.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 And if the wound is large and wide, especially when located in one of the triangular intestines, there must be no remedy nor health, only subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or when it occurs
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Every wound or abscess, when it becomes old, is universally called "fistula," especially when it opens and bleeds.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	 And a fistula follows incorrect nourishment that is hard and pale, where there is no pain, and it swells like the feathers of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	 and sometimes clear bowels, and other times thickened;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	 and at times scarce, and at other times sufficient;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	 And I have spoken in the division of wounds, that any wound not healed has no cure unless by one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	 It is to be understood, by the insufficiency of blood or body.
ou por sa malice;	 Or due to its own malignity.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	 Or because there is hard cure within, and under the lips, that it does not allow blood to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	 Or because there is too much boweling.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	 When the bone is fractured, and the material is of poor quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	 Or when the medicines are not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	 Or because corruption is a form of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	 Or due to the property in that region being slow digestion and delayed health, and fleeing by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	 Or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments with medicine in the section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to inform you of the treatment of a fistula that is done by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	 Say that abscess occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	 because there are abscesses that come from large veins and arteries, nerves, or the liver, intestines, bladder, some ribs, spine of the back, or any joint in hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 And if there is pain coming to the principal member's property, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	 And all types of fistulas that are of this kind have poor healing, with only effort and ignorance involved.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	 And if there is no fistula that reaches the location I have mentioned, and you trust in its healing, and witness it coming to light, then take a tent of wool or iron, if the fistula is straight.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	 And if the fistula is twisted, then search for a subtle tent of lead, because the lead sinks and bends around the twist.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	 And if the fistula has openings and you cannot properly search for it with tenting, then cleanse by enema through one of the openings, as moisture quickly moves from one opening to another, and cleanses.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	 Then skillfully use your power, to know if there is bone or nerve, and see how deeply it's cut into, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressing with your hand, and where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	 And when you truly know how deep it is, and if it's far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any of those places I have mentioned to you, then proceed as I have instructed you, and remove the broken bone and the corrupted cartilage within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	 And then heal it as much as possible, and if the abscess is well deep in its right place, you must cut into it fully, as far as you can see, then insert threaded ligatures with medicinal vinegar up to the top of the abscess until the medicine erodes the excess that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then apply balms with holy herbs until it becomes sound.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And if it does not heal with this, then proceed as we have described to cauterize; and if the bone is corrupted by an abscess, protect accordingly.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	 If veins or nerves do not trouble you or principal limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackening, treat with holy herbs until it becomes sound.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	 And if it does not heal, and the bowing remains as before; know that you must not go beyond this.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	 if exposed and festering, cleanse until reaching the bottom, remove all decay, then return it to its place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 And if it is thus healed, well done.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	 If not, know that the infection is too deep, you cannot address it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	 if there is no other remedy than applying heat naturally.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	 and if there is a small corrupted bone that you can extract with pincers, remove it using an appropriate instrument, and if there are many bones, extract all of them without leaving any.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 and if moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, strip the flesh and bone and separate the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	 And if you cannot remove them all at once, place an unpleasant substance to prevent decay on the wound, and leave it until flesh grows around the bones, then they will have easier access to the bones.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	 And if it is a large bone, like that of the leg or thigh, so thoroughly eradicate the decay until all the darkness has turned to bone, then repair the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	 And if there is a large part of it affected by decay, and it reaches close to the mole of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	 If it needs to be cut away and covered up all the way to the decay, then heal until it is solidified.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And I will tell you of an abscess that occurred in the leg of a man, so take example and assistance from your craftsmanship.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	 He was a youth under thirty years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause that came out of the body, as the substances reached the leg and were expelled through a large abscess, without any cause to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	 But the wise men worked so much on the abscess that it opened up, and they used a lot of materials, which then became an ulcer, causing great discharge and wetness throughout the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	 And many wise men attempted to heal it within two years, and there was no successful treatment in the art of hands until I came upon them, and saw the leg and the remedies with which they treated him, as the discharge affected much of his body.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 And the body of the youth turned red, and had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I pitched a tent in one of those places, and then searched all the places, finding that each came toward the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	 So I proceeded quickly and examined one of the discharges until I discovered a piece of bone, which was found to be decayed and porous, with the infection reaching deep into the bone.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	 I saw what appeared to be a rotten bone, and thought there was no other corruption except that which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	 And began to heal the wound with powerful medicines for long periods, but could not close it.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	 And then I resumed the treatment, and found the bone as before, discovered continued corruption in the bone, removed it, extracted it, and attempted to close the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	 But I couldn't remove all within an inch of the bone, and it rebelled against everything, so I then treated it with medicines again.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 And it became clean and closed quickly, and did not need to resume the treatment except due to the weakness of the patient who couldn't endure more, and because of my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the evacuation of blood often makes him groan, but he was wholeheartedly healthy, and in place of the bone grew a hard callus, which was well-disposed and had no harm or contrary effect at all, neither coming nor going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	 And if the bone is broken at any place on the body, it must be treated as follows:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	 Take hold of the ligament, and stretch to the head of the fractured bone, and command that no one stretches it upward.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	 And place another thicker ligament alongside the first, and tie it above the cartilage that is over the bone, and extend the head, such that you remove any corrupted cartilage from below, and reveal the cartilage at the location where you need to work, ensuring not to damage the cartilage.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	 And place a knife or a spatula below the bone to scrape off the corrupted cartilage.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And it must be done as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and do so again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	 If the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in a joint or part of it, expose all the flesh.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	 Then apply a hot compress off, and then connect the part with another of the corruption, and let it be as long as the corruption allows, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	 And if the corruption is in the joint, cut out the corrupted joint, and connect the bone where it was located on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	 And if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, there should be no other aid than coping.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	 And if the corruption is at the wrist of the hand or foot, it is a very strong thing, but nonetheless you must inquire about that corrosion and how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	 And clean it in all ways you can, but let neither vein nor nerve oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	 and know that the cutting instruments and needles to repair these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	 and therefore it is necessary to equip each type of work with its instrument.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	 and know that the work will show you which instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this craft, and the testimony of the ways of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 if you consider the instrument needed as it should be.
dou feu	If by fire.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	 The head may dislocate from within or due to weakness;

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of an abscess of a nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	 Pus is an abscess that arises from under the fingernail of the hand or toe, or sometimes occurs in other joints.

et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 And it reaches to the bone causing intense putrid pain, and the toe joint is swollen, and the skin turns black.

Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	 The treatment with iron is done in two ways:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	 One way is to cover them and bleed the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 And the other manner is to lift the vein, and pull it all through.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	 The size should be according to this method:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	 The first step involves the leg with very hot water, until the veins are sufficiently dilated, then hold the leg gently by pulling it from above the hip to below the buttocks.

et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And the treatment is as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	 The form of iron used to make the cautery must be curved and not sharp so that it does not cut the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 and is of large thickness, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but be broad as we have said, here is the form.
de la voinne civile	 Of the civil vein. (Note: This phrase may refer to
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	 This vein is situated in legs, warm areas where no plants or trees grow, and on land that lacks moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, which happens from swelling that arises beneath the skin, as it does internally with serpents and worms, embedded between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 When the signs of this vein's beginning are such that it comes in the leg as a great swelling, then the lump changes, and the vein begins to bulge outward, like a plant root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	 When the head is opened, it must be wrapped with a bandage of lin cloth about one and a half yards up to two yards along the leg, leaving the bandage on the limb, and each time there are no stitches left undone, wrap it again around the bandage.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	 And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and then wrap the remaining portion, but do not cover it entirely at its root until completely removed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	 because if you cut it, it may enter the heart and cause an abscess or decay there, leading to a severe illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	 for this reason, it must be treated little by little up to the root, and nothing or any part of the core should remain.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	 and this vein should never be treated when it's length reaches V or X hands, and a man came to me with one of such lengths, and when you cut it, it bleeds I or II drops, and the wound goes through to the bottom, causing everything in it to flow out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 And let the matter within be emptied, and bring suitable herbal remedies daily for a day, then treat as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	 And never strike the vein with your hand until it opens in the joint of the foot or toe, and when it bleeds profusely, and the blood flows out.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 Then treat as we have previously mentioned.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 And from worms that arise between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	 This disease is called in our land "ox disease," because it often occurs in the veins, and is a small worm that arises between skin and flesh, moving up and down throughout the body, feeling painfully as it passes through muscles until it pierces the skin where it travels, and bleeds profusely.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	 And it is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, such as those coming from worms and snails and ascarids or belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	 And there is doubt about its nature because when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and reaches the brain, by chance returns, and destrocks the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	 And this occurs many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	 When you see it being treated and drawn out, one cannot force it when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	 So it is necessary to bind the area above and below a strong joint tightly, then cut into and draw out thick matter, and if you cannot reach it entirely in its place, burn with fire on top until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	 And the greatest harm it causes is that they run a fever, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	 and if you see it coming or near the eyes, firmly pull out the eyebrows, then cut around them, and tether.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 And it is necessary to use the patient of bodily purification with dissolving medicaments for bad humours, and wash off putrid meats.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 From the pain which arises from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	 This disease is called "wakeyre" in our land, and it brings pain to certain limbs, then moves from member to member.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	 I was called to an unwell woman, and discovered some swollen arms, and saw a small inflammation in the vein of her arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	 And shortly after, the vein rises as if on a shoulder, more quickly than anything else, like silver when it falls from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	 The pain departs from that spot, and spreads to the shoulder, and then shortly after courses throughout the entire body, until it reaches the opposite arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 Then he told me that it returned within his body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	sofle a lisso:
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	 Nevertheless, I had wanted to make sure that the pain moved from one place to another, but I did not see it in the woman as I observed.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	 and I thought that this was because the woman had dry veins, with open wounds, and thus appeared to be bloated.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 And they do not appear according to this reason for those who are diabetic, and who have moist bodies and veins restored.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	 And when you see that this disease needs curing, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, then scrape above and below swiftly, and afterwards cover until the inflammation subsides.
et cauterize le leu;	 and cauterize thereafter.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat as for those who are troubled by inflammation, like rotten pills, and pills of iron ore, and similar things.
des saiettes	 Of arrowheads
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrowheads are diverse, depending on their appearance and the way they pierce the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	 The variety in them is that there are those who have large points, small points, hairy ones, and smooth ones.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	 And of those with two edges, and of those with tongues, and of those with projections.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	 and that which flows in no limb, it flows according to the following methods:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 or in principal limbs such as the brain, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	 When it flows thus in no part of these limbs, the sign of death that I will tell you hereafter is evident:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	 if it must be considered for the extraction of this arrowhead, as death comes afterward in various conditions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 and when these bad signs are not evident, and the arrowhead is not completely embedded, then treat it as such, and care for the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	 When the arrowhead enters and penetrates the bone near the brain, causing a hollow behind it on the skull, which is when blindness occurs along with numbness, trembling and reddening of the eyes, and inflammation and red tongue, spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	 and sometimes it is without force in the nose or ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	 and occasionally it affects speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	 and the wound appears as white hair-like growths, and heals like blood from a wound.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 If these signs appear to you, pursue the treatment, and extract the arrowhead if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	 When the sign of the arrow as it passes or enters the body, is near the left arm, and feels similarly as if it had been driven into a hard object, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	 and perhaps the arrow moves like hairs, with black blood flowing outward, accompanied by coldness, pale sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 Thus they have doubts that death will follow.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of arrow wound is that without clear foam from the wound's exit, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	 And if the arrow penetrates into the fleshy part of the buttocks, it is near the small intestines;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	 and spills a great amount of blood, causing severe pain and groaning;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 and they move all the limb joints in the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	When an arrow falls or lodges in the stomach, if it comes from the wound, then no part of the digested flesh is spared.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow falls or lodges in the stomach and does not pierce any part of the intestines on its exit, there is no hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	 And if the arrow penetrates into the bladder, causing urine to leak and flow out, and the patient feels intense pain;
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 The wound appears to be fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as made by the fingers and knuckles and throat and shoulder and elbow and spine of the back and neck and thighs, and similar members are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the shaft is in a nerve or artery and it is not poisonous as I will tell you of how it happened to me, so that you may do similarly.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	 It happened to a man whose arrow struck the knee near its root.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 I tried it, and injured it on the other side through the ear fat, but was not severely damaged.

li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 The joint remained sound, and nothing adverse occurred to it.

je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 I shaved the beard, and acted discreetly as long as it was necessary, and the Christians were safe.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	 And deceived an arrow into one of them, which was lodged in his belly, and believed he would die.

et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 And I appeared to have found the path of the arrow.

et il le me dist.	 And he told it to me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	 I applied the medicinal acrid water to the wound by hand until it was opened, and tried closing it, and felt the arrowhead at its intended place.

et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	 and it passed through completely within four months, and then I loosened the wound so that I could insert pincers on both sides, but it couldn't be removed.
