mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 but the wise master physician compares little about many things, and focuses on what is currently happening and failing; he provides nine works of knowledge and nine instruments for handling strange occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	 I say that arrows come from limbs where they are embedded, according to two ways.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	 or by their entry point, or from another direction;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 and those that enter through the same opening they entered from are arrowheads in living flesh, and will do so again at no time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	 And if it does not come out now, leave it as long as the flesh is rotting around it and there is pus coming from the wound.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	 And similarly if it is embedded in bone and cannot come out, leave it as such for some days, changing its position each day.

If the arrow is not lodged solenly in the bone and does not reach the joint, and the patient experiences no major change for some days, then attempt to extract it.

puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the wound until it heals cleanly.

et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	 And if you can feel it, remove using any suitable instrument.

et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And place the patient as they were when the arrow fell upon them, for that is their greatest help, and if you cannot do so, then put them according to what signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	 The arrow that comes from another direction or pierces something of theirs, or where the skin is swollen can be seen or felt distinctly.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	 So cut accordingly as long as the pincers can grip it, and then extract it:

Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if held within the bone, rotate your round hand so that it enters the bone, then widen the bone before extracting it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	 And if it cannot come out, let it remain for now, then resume extraction until it comes out completely.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	 and if the arrowhead remains in it, you must remove the entire shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	 and if it breaks off, you should administer binding, and if the instrument is a knife, such that the tip of the arrow enters into the handle of the tool.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 and then remove it completely, and if the arrowhead is loose, place the instrument with its point inserted to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 If the arrowhead is contaminated, it is necessary to cut out all surrounding tissue where the poison resides, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	 And if the arrowhead breaks or pierces the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is recent, you may cover up, as needed.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	 And be careful not to puncture the vein or nerve, then extract it, and then close the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 and perform the treatment until it is healed completely.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pliers used to extract arrows resembles an eagle's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	 And there are many ways to do so:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 large, medium, and small, depending on the quantity of the arrowheads.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The form of the pointed hair is also like the feather of a bird, to direct it towards the tip of the arrowhead, as shown here.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of pincers for both setting and retrieving:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of common bodily veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	 There are veins to be opened that have XXXI in total, sixteen heads included, which are as follows:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	 II jugulars located behind the ears, called the double "herbeck".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	 and the two arteries that are visible in both temples.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	 and two veins that are in the groins of both eyes, called "inspire".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	 And the vein that lies within the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	 and the vein that is at the temple, near the hairline;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	 and the two temples which are on either side of the head;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	 and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are called "Egoheirich" veins.
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	 The veins of which there are commonly five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	 One is on the head, and it's to the left ribcage side, and they call it "the vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	 The other is named "fast", and it's composed of the head and abdominal parts, and they call it by the local name "vein of the body".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The abdominal part is to the right ribcage side and they call it by the local name "vein of the belly", and it's below the navel, and this one where blood can be drawn, clearly shown at the top of the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	 And the small vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two streams.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	 And in the leg where there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	 One is located below the hollow of the left breast bone, and the second (joint) which is at the ankle of the right leg.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	 and the vein called "sne," which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 and in the other leg are three veins below those (joints).
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	 The sting from the veins that are after the ears can cause old headaches and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	 and the quality of this sting, as I have told you, is to raise the head of the patient, and rub the area or veins with a coarse cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	 then tighten the neck of the patient with a winding motion until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places above the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	 When you find the knots on your fingers, and where you feel hairs under your finger, beware of them.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	 Then take the lancet and puncture from under the vein to the bone, then lift your hand up along the entire vein, and cut and remove the skin and vein clean until you see blood.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 Then strain it tightly, as long as it is cleansed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 and I have already said the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	 The cleaning of the two arteries that are in both temples should be done with an ancient, hardened, and accustomed practice for tears from the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	 And the quality of the surgeon is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	 and it must be that the patient keeps his head distant, until both veins are clearly visible.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	 and feels pain from under your elbow, then securely tie (a tourniquet).
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	 then lift the skin above your elbow to the second level of your elbow, and place the lance below it, then lift the vein up, and cover it, just as you did with two other veins, and control the bleeding according to necessity.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	 then lay the patient down, and place your elbow over the vein for an hour, then cover with cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 and bandage firmly, leaving it until healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 And we have discussed this in their care and extraction, which begins the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	 The bandage of the vein on the forehead is worth as much as that for headaches from ancient face diseases, and migraines, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	 And its quality is such that the patient should turn his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 Then take the instrument called "Fossor", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	 And place its tip on the vein, and pierce under your hand or another object, allowing the blood to flow out according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein until it is neither slanted nor bent at a wide angle of the flesh.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	 However, it must not be too tight;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 And the ligament across it, for the bone is close by, and sometimes it breaks the membranes when they are delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	 The ligaments of the veins that are in the joints should be supported with bandages and to the tendon, redness, yellowness, and swelling in oil, and illnesses of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	 And the quality of these ligaments is that the patient twists their neck by pulling at any attachment, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Then the bandage and be sure to have the ligament across it, a little long and wide membrane, for there is no irritation.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	 And if the membranes are delicate, they may sometimes break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 Then let there be sufficient bloodletting as needed, and then apply linen, and secure it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	 The vein of the nose if it becomes congested should be treated with cold water and soothing ointments, as well as face ailments such as migraines and redness that occur on the face, especially when they are longstanding.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	 The quality of the congestion is such that it causes the patient's neck to be strained. Then straighten its nose with your left hand and take a long, fine thread through between the two nostrils, as the vein does not open easily, so the blood will begin to flow immediately.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	 And do not pull too hard initially, and let the blood flow according to your necessity, then tie it off for a night, as it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 And this is the form of a blowfly
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	 The straining of the sinews assists in extending ligaments, and at the beginning of leprosy, as well as many other diseases, scabs, corrosion, herpes, and itching.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	 and the quality of straining is that it pulls away the patient's neck from both sides, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	 and the master stands over the patient's head, then slices slightly on both sides, then straighten the vein a bit widely, then quickly cut the blood as needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	 Then make another incision on the other vein, then loosen the ligaments, and strain both veins moderately so that the patient does not become strangled.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 And let it remain until morning, so that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	 of the liver inflammation
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of vein lips above contributes to wounds in the mouth, and decay of gums, and tears of lips, and ulcers and abscesses.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	 And the nature of the healing is for you to seat the patient before you and hold his neck as I have instructed.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	 Then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one is in the right lip and the other in the left, and recognize them by what they are black, and by the small black veins surrounding them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 So then cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them, or you are in doubt, cut the larger one from each side, and likewise for all veins above and below, because they are of a similar manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 for inflammation underneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	 The healing of the veins below the tongue helps after the cerebral healing, and it is during the extension of the throat, and for eye diseases and mouth ailments. (Note: This line might contain typographical errors or be difficult to translate due to historical medical terminology not aligning with modern understanding.)
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	 And the quality of the saigner is that the patient bleeds between their hands in front of the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks down either side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 Now clean both, and do not cut too deep, as from there are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	 The veins of the arm that are commonly bled have two methods of practice:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	 or by poking through all along with a wide lancet blade, or olive oil subtly as sharp cutters are called "anise.";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 And they are wide and subtle according to the breadth and length of the veins.;
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the wormwood is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	 It is necessary to open plain-haired veins with abundant visible blood that contains thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And this is the form of the olive bile.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and are more subtly pointed, and suitable for tying up fine veins where there is subtle lemon-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	 The saintliness of the basilica, which is one of these veins, assists in diseases that are from the throat, and neck, and groin, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 And it is fitting for the physician to bleed properly, and that he washes from the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	 And if it comes out of the artery, and a stream of blood flows, then he should staunch it as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And the bile must not be sharp but cut evenly as I mentioned.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	 And if the vein does not open clearly, then one should extract it and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	 or you want any hair from it, or bleed into the vein within its arm.
elle apert manifestement;	 It becomes clearly apparent;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 and the sore at the nape of the neck as we have mentioned.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	 And if you see the lie of the sinew, then as I say, when you raise the arm, gently touch the head until you recognize the hairs.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	 then sign your name at the top of the parchment and then lift the arm, treat the vein at the nape of the neck.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	 and be careful not to injure the artery when you see the head swelling, for it is the artery:
eschui la donques.	 flee then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	 And if you see it bulging as well like the urine of a child, and the flesh is red and tender, know that this is from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	 Quickly proceed, then place your hand underneath for a while, and afterwards straighten out the arm which is bent. This often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	 ties the arm together, and leaves it like that, so the patient does not move it.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And there is fear of death, so do not move until he is well again.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	 And if the arm is not straightened out and it heals, and there are no medicines provided, then cut the artery in case of rupture, as they retract.
et estainche li sans.	 and straighten the arm.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And take a piece of willow bark, break it, and choose one half to tie up securely until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	 if the arm is straightened out properly, that's good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	 If this does not work, apply the treatment with powders that coagulate blood as we have said.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And the coagulation is not always in various positions due to the slight location of the wound and the strength of the joints on the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	 The action of the vein is such that it transports blood above and below, because it consists of the basilic and cephalic vessels, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	 And it is necessary for the physician to examine below the nerve, and if too much pressure is applied, then the nerve can be damaged, causing swelling and severe pain, and sometimes cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	 And this nerve can be found many times, and if it is not in any places due to its subtlety, one must explore with the dilator instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 And escape the nerve at your will.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is blood between the two veins, it flows for a long time.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	 The heating of the skull helps to draw blood towards the head and benefits the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 And it is proper to heat by touching the area of the olive or myrtle fruit, as it's the safest among all treatments because there are no nerves or arteries there.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	 However, you must choose the lightest one to apply and do not put anything if it's the first time, then repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 And sometimes it causes swelling in some men when applied for the first time, but it does not harm them.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of this disease is according to what you think.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	 The first thing you must know about heating is that it's not performed just to maintain health but also to avoid future diseases.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	 And there is to be made a suture on one of the three veins present.
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	 that is, namely the cephalic, saphenous, and basilica.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	 And it should be sutured at the beginning of pre-prandial fasting and in autumn and winter after eating when signs of repletion appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 And it should be sutured on the first day or third, after two to three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	 The suture applied for diseases has no fixed time, but when needed it is by day or night, at all hours and times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 And one should not suture children until 14 years old, nor women carrying a fetus from the fourth month up to seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not let them exercise too much if they are old men who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	 And when anyone wishes to purge themselves in any way, it is necessary that they cleanse the intestines with a mild enema, if there is much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw the excess from the intestines which could harm the main members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	 Nor should those who are too greedy on meats nor drunkards, no matter how much they are so, or have dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	 and one should purge after an attack of colic, vomiting, abdominal distention, frequent intercourse with a woman or traveling, staying up late and conjugal relations, and whatever the rest, whether by something from weapons or the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	 Then subtly manage the humors, if they are large, through meats, drinks, and medicines, if you have permission to do so.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	 Then enter a bath if nothing prevents it, to subtly manage the blood and cleanse the vein near the wound.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	 And keep clear of work, pain, leisure, and such things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	 And be tied and raised, and let the healer stand higher than the patient being treated, then rub the arm two or three times, and then stretch out the ligaments moderately, for if it is too tight or loose, one cannot correct the humors.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	 Then rub his entire body with hands until the veins become inflamed and are felt.

des sainies de ventouse	 Removal of pus-filled abscesses
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	 Vents are made of horns, or glasses, or vermilion.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	 And the procedure is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 By striking and drawing blood, or feeling struck.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	 And this inflammation which causes a feeling of being struck occurs in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	 Or it is with great heat, or feels like fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	 And inflammation that occurs by striking and blood extraction happens in fourteen parts of the body, so one is completely at the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	 And the other is near the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	 And two others are in the ribs of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	 And the inflammation below the chin.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	 And the inflammaturities of both shoulders.
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	 And the inflammations over the heels.
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	 And the inflammations within both arms.
et les ventouses des II jambes;	 And the inflammations in both legs.
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	 And the inflammations at both ankles.
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	 And the bleeding does not produce much blood, but from tiny veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not bother anyone, as with normal vein bleeding.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And it does not require any treatment, nor heat or cold application, in no disease that arises from excessive eating, as long as all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	 And if it is necessary due to diseases or habits, we provide each injection at the beginning or end of the month, and before and after every hour.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	 because there are those who, when they need injections, feel heavy sensations;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	 and for those who experience fullness and reddening on their face, head, neck, and darkening of the eyes.

et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if it is so, use watercress oil, or of lily, or chamomile, or similar substances.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excesses are large and cold, take oil of wormwood, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if for the one you are treating with a tender and broad bandage, do not put any oil on it, but after ventosation with rosewater, or cold water, or elderberry water, or gourd juice, or pearl ash solution, or any similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with much moisture should rise easily, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	 And those who have excessive swelling rise with old wine, or of boiled watercress, or of anise or chamomile infusion, or similar substances.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	 and they must not be saunaed before the bath nor after the bath but one hour to two hours later.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 and should not sleep after saunaing, and it is necessary that they sweat, when they need to be saunaed and once they are saunaed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	 And watch for those who are pale from cholera, and whose skin is too dry and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	 If it becomes necessary, they should take cold things such as red apples, endives, lettuces and similar items.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 and mild spices, and lamb fat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	 And those with a cold disposition should take honey syrup, and moderately aged wine, along with some spices, mild spices, small birds, and partridge.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	 and on the day they exercise, should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	 and it is advisable to give certain individuals neither triacle nor musk before or after vomiting to strengthen the main body parts.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 Be subtle with them, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	 The cupping that is applied without causing injury are those placed over the liver, and joints, and gout, and abdomen, buttocks, legs, and groin, because these limbs do not tolerate being pierced or punctured anywhere, it is only done to draw blood from one part of the body to another, as we place on wounds when they are healing.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	 for removing swelling that is in the limb, as we apply cupping to the abdomen and buttocks to reduce the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	 and alleviate pain when there is edema or stones, and remove them by its attractive property, possibly removing the edema or returning the stone to its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	 And so it is done when placing over the liver and kidney where there is retained wind-swelling, and these blisters are prepared empty to drain as needed.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 And never are they prepared together with fire, nor with plain water as in some diseases of the chest, and thusly you fill the blister with hot water poultice or with water that has boiled medicinal herbs for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form for administering a cauterizing agent is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	 And it should have two sides each half a palm wide and with a tiny puncture within the center like to piercing with a needle, made of silver before so that it does not harm the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	 And have at hand a rod of crossbow or iron to insert a candlewick while they are large and small depending on the diseases and condition of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 because children's cupping is different from that for adults, and for thin individuals as opposed to fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	 And so one must place this cupping on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	 take the candle of wax or lubricant and place it inside the cupping over the rod that is also within the cupping, so that the light shines to the bottom of the cupping without burning the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	 and then place it on the limb, and you should do so at the points we have mentioned, so that when desired, steam will form, and remove the cupping.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And you take the lining as before, and often it recurrences if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	 In the ventouse used for treating pleurisy, which is filled with water at once, has neither penis nor outlet, and is only managed when full of water, and placed on the limb fully.
et c’est li forme:	 And it is formed as follows:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	 Suction cups are managed only where you cannot place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, for example.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	 And on the heels of horses, whether hooves or nails, and others like them;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	 And its quality is such that when you find those without stains which are in soft clear waters with some slime, then take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	 and place them into a clean, soft water source until they become accustomed to it, and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	 then make them safe from veins and pus, then rub the member until it is reddened, and place the previously cleaned stones there.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 and when they have sunk and settled, if it is possible to place them near an outlet, then do so, for this is highly beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	 If not, raise it easily and then expose to water very well, and then squeeze out the liquid.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	 If too much blood is left in the body after removing the stones, then wipe with a linen cloth dipped in cold water and place it there until the stone has been squeezed out.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	 If there are multiple abscesses, apply crushed vitriol or galewacke, and similar substances, until they are healed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	 Or place it on the middle of scraped fleshe, and leave them until they have healed at the lee, now seal.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 And if you need more remedy, then take other substances.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	 And if the substances do not take effect, then rub the flesh with fresh blood or place a needle until the abscess comes out, and then apply them to it, and soon as they feel the blood, let them heal.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And when you see that they bleed, then powder with a bit of aloe and sea salt, or ash, so they will now heal.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine and involve the restoration of breaks and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	 Learn well, dear student, that the foolish do not delve into this chapter's wisdom, for they have never seen any ancient books or read their letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	 and therefore, knowledge is scarce in our land, as I've found no good examples of it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	 and I know little about it, though through the wisdom of ancient books which I have studied thoroughly, by experience, and from my life's habits.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 and I have described in this chapter what is contained within it, shortened at the end, and clearly shown the forms of inflammations that are produced, as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary therefore that we say here the preface of this book containing the essence and chapters in which the sage applies his understanding, dwelling on truth so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	 I say that when any breakage or dislocation, twisting, or contortion occurs in a limb, you must support the injured side of the patient with parts weak due to childhood, age, or frailty.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	 If the tension is not too much, or too cold.
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	 And mixing with cold things, that is to say, cold baths, and fodder for birds and horses, do not drink wine or eat any fatty meats, and do not fill up too much on foods that fill the veins with blood, until you no longer have doubt of a hot abscess or material spreading in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 If it comes to the patient being so weakened again that they cannot be governed as before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient with foods that promote nourishment, such as wheat cooked in water, rice, barley, sheep's stomach, eggs, fresh fish, rich wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For proper nourishment allows for faster healing of the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	 And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well healed or united according to their nature for limb strengthening, nor those as tender as children's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	 But do not worry, reset above the broken bone with strong ligaments that join the limb together, until it is restored as if it were before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And do not finish all of your work, and for this reason you should nourish on large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a head fracture is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter about all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are fractures that occur from dislocation, and others by being bent, as with the breaking of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with an open wound, and a crack throughout a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	 And each method has its means, and its proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory brings in that place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	 And is known the fracture of the bone by what the twist is present, and opened widely due to force, and it presses near the palm.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	 And when there is no twist or touching of it, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 However, it may well have twisting, or splitting, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	the in sone de pru;
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And know that the fractures which curve upward, and are two parts dislocated, they must now be aligned evenly, so as to abscesses when they arise.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	 and if abscesses occur, leave it for no day until the abscess is eased.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	 then make it even with movements that you can lightly and easily perform, knowing that its restoration is easier than those of others where there are missing pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 then straighten it if necessary afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	 And if the bone has broken pieces, and is separated into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or on your hand, if it's small limbs, or at II tendons, or at one tendon and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	 And place the member according to its natural shape, so that when parts of the injured limb are dislocated, you reset them by any means necessary and guide it back into position as best as you can, ensuring that through your work no injury or pain befalls the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And properly set the two ends of the bones according to their best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	 And if you feel that it does not heal well with your hand, then... (Please provide additional context or text for continuation)
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 If the dressing is done well and do not strain it too much, nor compress as those who cause abscesses to boil and contract in their limbs, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	 And when the limb is at risk of infection, so treat the patient well to ensure it does not move, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning or otherwise. (Note: It seems there might be a missing part of the text here for proper continuation)
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And ensure the limb is so securely fixed that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	 For when it feels no pain, not even slightly, and then it must be put in such a position that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	 and ensure that it is placed correctly, so that any twisting does not occur when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 and the quality of the broken limb depends as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Seek knowledge that broken limbs vary in minor and major ways, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	 For there are small members, such as fingers and toes:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	 If necessary, wrap soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	 and those that are large, like thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	 if it is necessary to bind with a wide and sturdy bandage, as the wide bandages can encompass the entire large limb evenly, without any unevenness.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	 then place three or four light pads (or as needed depending on the limb), and tie one end to the entire bandage, then go above the fracture and make it tighter there than at the break, moving away slightly from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	 and soften the bandage a little at a time until you cover most of the healthy part again, then take another bandage and wrap around directly above the fracture site.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	 Then return to the part below the fracture and strain it gently, not too hard or weakly, as we have said in the first section above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 Then place between the splints linen or cloth so that they are all equal, then bind it above with bandages, and then put well-made supports underneath if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	 And if there is an abscess or swelling, then place something soothing on the abscess and that removes the swelling, leaving it as such for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 Then strain the supports and make pads of a piece about one hand's breadth thick, or of wood used for making shingles, or of palm fronds, according to this pattern:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	 But it is necessary for the stake that someone places on the fracture to be a bit larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	 and so long as needed for the member's smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	 then fasten the stakes in the same way as you did with the first fracture, and later over time, using a thread as in the initial treatment of the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	 the tighter it is, the less there will be;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	 and it should be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 because if the thread is too thick as I have seen in works of folks who make their rope cords from twisted flax threads, and it's a significant error, for the fracture cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it should not have less than two inches between each stake.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is in pain from the head of an extremity after it has been tightened into its proper place, then apply linen or cotton padding under them so they do not slip.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by broken bones, I will describe the treatment for this afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And remember that it is not necessary to extract all fractured bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	 When the limb is large, one must not put staves unless after five or seven days, or more depending on the risk of abscess occurring soon.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	 and here is the method of ancient eyebolts to restore breaks, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 And take some flour that is held within the walls of the mill, and knead it with abundance of eggs, and use this concoction which should not be too clear or too thick; this is the common method for an eyebolt restoring a break in various positions, especially in women and small children, as it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	 Another way of applying a dressing that heals breaks, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	 Take oil of aloes, myrrh, nutsgrass juice, arabic gum, and honey, about 12 drachms.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	 Myrrh and aloes, about 5 drachms.
alechil VIIII З.;	 Alethinon (or another suitable astringent) VIIII drach
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	 And make the powder, and mix with honey and egg white.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 If the body's constitution is hot, utilize this plaster as it has good composition and quickly restores broken bones, benefiting many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	 Another form of plaster useful for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	 Take muscat and wormwood, soaked in strong wine.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 Myrrh and aloes, also infused with the same amount of wine as before (IX being a Roman numeral for 
acaice VI З.;	 Acacia and frankincense, likewise infused.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Armenian balsam (X liters), finely ground and mixed with either water or milk, to be administered.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	 Another form of plaster for joints and bones displaced from their place, alleviates acute pain, and is used to cut the bone, with fractures being addressed.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Take new linen, and soak it with ease and oil cooked, and place it at the location.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 These dressings do not restore, but are beneficial for cooling of abscesses and properly soothing the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	 Another method to mend broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, mix them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method for dressing to restore bone fractures and ease remaining abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	 Take wormwood root, chamomile, flowers of violets, wheat flour, each one in equal parts;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 and grind it up, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, then apply with fresh coriander water or plain water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way to treat more effectively than the first, when an abscess comes with member restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	 Take wormwood roots, flax seeds, balm, melilotus (sweet clover), and senna, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 And it is bruised, and concocted with salt water or soft water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should not place anything above the broken limb to promote healing except a mixture of wax and oil, and nothing else, and it must be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen suggests placing dry and slightly warm substances on the broken limb to promote healing, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have mentioned before.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	 Other way of dressing appropriate for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Take musk and chervil from chopped men's nether regions or bird feathers, wormwood, and saffron in equal amounts; grind them up and make a plaster with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	 And then leave the dressing on for some time, and be cautious that the patient feels no pain or has moved any bones in their place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	 If not removed after a few days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	 And if pain comes to the place or itching, feeling of restlessness or swelling occurs, hurry, remove the dressing and take off the plaster now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	 And take light cloth, and sponge of sea water moistened, and immerse it in clear water, and raise the place where the pain exists, until the itching ceases and the pain is eased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	 Then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply a dry cloth wrung in clear water or rose oil and bind it with a bandage, until you are sure of a hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	 And rest the swelling of the limb and ease its pain, then resume subtle manipulation and a bit of opium, but do not bind it as tightly as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And proceed delicately until it is safe.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and painful and swollen throughout the limb, and you need opium and ligature, then proceed as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	 And if nothing comes to the limb as we have said, do not dislocate it unless after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	 And never leave it XX days, as one sees, until the breaker is ready, and approach the shoulder joint above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	 Then initially reset again, and the injured area swells with flesh, as I have said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	 And if you see it drying more than necessary, know that infections cannot come there.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	 Then the patient must take warm water baths whenever you release it, and do so every day, and wash a little more frequently.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	 Through this treatment thus prevent infections on the member and quickly heal what foolish doctors have done, returning the limb incorrectly.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 It is wrong and such actions are fearsome; I see nothing else but laziness and working improperly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	In various ways of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	 Many ways of fractures are, with diverse shapes, and their causes distinguished.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	 because there are fractures made by the blow of a sword, and the bone splits through all the bone up to its facet which is from under the bone, as if it were an axe or club.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 and therefore this kind of fracture is called "axing".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	 Or the sword cuts through the bone from above, and this type of fracture is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 and there are wounds from these large or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, or split or crack of stone-like bone, or falling on stone, or other such things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is persistent bleeding, which reaches up to the tela under the bone, or above it, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	 And if there is a wound that fills the bone as subtly as hairs, and it is a small crack, and therefore this type of fracture is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	 And if the wound is made by being struck with a stone, or falling, or similar thing, and allows entry of the bone shard, making the head appear as hot crossbows do when fired on their targets.
si entre li piere dedens.	 If within the flesh beneath.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	 And it happens more in those who have bones underneath that are as soft as an infant's skull;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	 And occurs in all these ways of fractures where small pieces are dislocated as such.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And I shall speak of them right there.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all ways of fractures by distraction upon them, and examination with probes, and through the corrupted cartilage that is beneath.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The resemblance of hair is known by what happens when the bone is uncovered and rubbed well over it; thus there appears black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a breakage, beware if any unfortunate incident occurs with the patient; and if you see no evil event like vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, palpitations, fever ague, eyes exiting forcefully and reddening, and other such manifestations in various dispositions, do not heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no hopeless incident, and expect a remedy, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the pain first comes to you, and it is in winter, one must remove the bone by the fourteenth day when the moon can be seen.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you must hasten to remove the bone by the seventh day before the fleshing around the bone becomes corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	 And if the bone fracture comes near the cloth that covers the brain, it is necessary to split the broken part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	 and it is that you grasp the wounded head, expose over the bone in all ways you can, and on top of the wound's shape as gently as possible, if bleeding occurs upon exposing the bone or abscesses appear, then aid with whatever is needed, and ensure the cavity is filled with wrung cloth soaked in oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	 and let the wound rest until all abscesses are eased, and be sure that bleeding ceases;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	 Then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to two methods of operation.
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 One method involves cutting a narrow section in front, thus shaping it as follows:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	 And the second method is to have various cuts, some narrow and others wide, with points and made of different iron types.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 and work lightly, not cutting into the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	 And if the bone is tough and hard, it must be pierced all around, as you make cuts with chisels, not perforating beyond the outer layer of the bone. There should be a margin or circle above the tip that does not allow the point to go through the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	 And you must have several tools so that each comes in its place for the examination of the bone, and you will have tongs for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 This is the form of the three kinds of tongs:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	 The quality for probing around the broken bone is to place one tongs on the bone and turn it with both hands until you know that the bone has been cut.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	 Then place the tongs elsewhere for a while, and do so all around it, then cut into the space between the fragments with incisors. Do this more delicately than possible, gently, as we have said, until you can feel the bone at your hand or on any of the tools that you hold like pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 And ensure you do not touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	 And when you have broken the bone and exposed it, if necessary to resect the protruding part of the bone that is attached to any other instrument similar to a chisel, but it must be much finer and more delicate than the other chisel.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	 and if there is nothing of small bones or scales remaining, then lightly rub with the appropriate instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	 And another way of treatment is what Galen prescribes, which is more subtle;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 and it should be done strongly, as he says.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you must expose a part of the bone where the break is most open. Once you have exposed that part, place the pointed end of this lenticular chisel on it as follows.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	 And do not cut deeply on one side, and it is a swollen area on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	 Then with a small mallet underneath, so that you gently strike the bone entirely through it, and be careful of the sinew that is above.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 If it is loose to the bone, strike the bone gently, for striking too hard can cause harm and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the skin and the bone is cut slightly above it so that there are small pieces, then you should treat the severity accordingly, and remove scales with a fine razor of which you must have various quantities in order to administer at each place what is most beneficial according to the work done and the shape of the fracture.
